"""
FREIGHTINFO_MARAD Runbook - Scraper
Extracts weekly vessel count data via Playwright pixel-scan of the BTS Tableau chart.

Strategy: Tableau "Highlight Selected Items" legend button is activated so only
one region's line is vivid (high colour saturation) at a time. For each x column
canvas.getImageData() finds the highest-saturation pixel (= highlighted line) and
the mouse is moved exactly there. Three passes (East / West / Gulf) give clean,
region-specific tooltips without any y-position guessing.
"""

import os
import re
import json
import logging
from datetime import datetime

import requests
from bs4 import BeautifulSoup
from playwright.sync_api import sync_playwright, TimeoutError as PWTimeout

import config

logger = logging.getLogger(__name__)

# ── JS: find highest-saturation pixel in canvas column x (= highlighted line) ──
_FIND_LINE_JS = """
(colX) => {
    var best = null, bestArea = 0;
    document.querySelectorAll('canvas').forEach(function(c) {
        var a = c.width * c.height;
        if (a > bestArea) { bestArea = a; best = c; }
    });
    if (!best) return null;
    var ctx = best.getContext('2d');
    if (!ctx) return null;
    var h = best.height;
    var data = ctx.getImageData(colX, 0, 1, h).data;
    var bestY = -1, bestSat = -1, bestR = 0, bestG = 0, bestB = 0;
    for (var y = 5; y < h - 5; y++) {
        var i = y * 4;
        var r = data[i], g = data[i+1], b = data[i+2], a = data[i+3];
        if (a < 80) continue;
        var mx = Math.max(r, g, b), mn = Math.min(r, g, b);
        if (mx === 0) continue;
        var sat  = (mx - mn) / mx;
        var luma = (r * 299 + g * 587 + b * 114) / 1000;
        if (sat > 0.15 && luma < 230 && sat > bestSat) {
            bestSat = sat; bestY = y; bestR = r; bestG = g; bestB = b;
        }
    }
    if (bestY < 0) return null;
    return { y: bestY, r: bestR, g: bestG, b: bestB, sat: Math.round(bestSat * 100) };
}
"""

# ── JS: poll tooltip for vessel data ──────────────────────────────────────────
_POLL_JS = """
() => {
    var sels = ['.tab-tooltip', '.tab-beautified-tooltip', '.tab-glass-content'];
    for (var s of sels) {
        var el = document.querySelector(s);
        if (el && el.innerText && el.innerText.includes('Vessels')) {
            return el.innerText.trim();
        }
    }
    return null;
}
"""


class FREIGHTINFOScraper:

    def __init__(self):
        self.session = requests.Session()
        self.session.headers.update({
            'User-Agent': 'Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) AppleWebKit/537.36 '
                          '(KHTML, like Gecko) Chrome/120.0.0.0 Safari/537.36'
        })

    # =========================================================================
    # WEEK MAPPING (epochconverter.com)
    # =========================================================================

    def fetch_week_data(self):
        """Fetch and cache week mapping data."""
        if os.path.exists(config.WEEK_CACHE_FILE):
            try:
                with open(config.WEEK_CACHE_FILE, 'r') as f:
                    data = json.load(f)
                if str(datetime.now().year) in data:
                    logger.info("Using cached week mapping data")
                    return True
            except Exception:
                pass

        logger.info("Fetching week mapping data from epochconverter.com...")
        current_year = datetime.now().year
        years = [current_year, current_year + 1, current_year + 2]
        week_data = {}

        for year in years:
            url = config.WEEK_URL_TEMPLATE.format(year=year)
            try:
                resp = self.session.get(url, timeout=15)
                resp.raise_for_status()
                soup = BeautifulSoup(resp.text, 'html.parser')
                table = soup.find('table', class_='infotable')
                if not table:
                    continue
                weeks = []
                for row in table.find('tbody').find_all('tr'):
                    cells = row.find_all('td')
                    if len(cells) < 3:
                        continue
                    try:
                        wk_match = re.match(r'Week\s+(\d+)', cells[0].get_text(strip=True))
                        if not wk_match:
                            continue
                        wk_num = int(wk_match.group(1))
                        f_date = datetime.strptime(
                            cells[1].get_text(separator=' ', strip=True), '%B %d, %Y'
                        ).strftime('%Y-%m-%d')
                        t_date = datetime.strptime(
                            cells[2].get_text(separator=' ', strip=True), '%B %d, %Y'
                        ).strftime('%Y-%m-%d')
                        weeks.append({'week': wk_num, 'from': f_date, 'to': t_date})
                    except Exception:
                        continue
                if weeks:
                    week_data[str(year)] = weeks
            except Exception as e:
                logger.warning(f"Failed to fetch week data for {year}: {e}")

        if week_data:
            with open(config.WEEK_CACHE_FILE, 'w') as f:
                json.dump(week_data, f, indent=2)
            return True
        return False

    # =========================================================================
    # BROWSER SETUP (Playwright)
    # =========================================================================

    def _make_browser(self, p):
        """Launch Playwright Chromium with anti-detection settings."""
        browser = p.chromium.launch(
            headless=config.HEADLESS_MODE,
            slow_mo=20,
            args=[
                '--disable-blink-features=AutomationControlled',
                '--no-sandbox',
                '--disable-features=IsolateOrigins,site-per-process',
            ]
        )
        context = browser.new_context(
            viewport={'width': 1440, 'height': 900},
            locale='en-US',
            timezone_id='America/New_York',
            user_agent=(
                'Mozilla/5.0 (Windows NT 10.0; Win64; x64) '
                'AppleWebKit/537.36 (KHTML, like Gecko) '
                'Chrome/149.0.0.0 Safari/537.36'
            ),
            extra_http_headers={
                'Accept': 'text/html,application/xhtml+xml,application/xml;q=0.9,*/*;q=0.8',
                'Accept-Language': 'en-US,en;q=0.9',
                'sec-ch-ua': '"Google Chrome";v="149", "Chromium";v="149", "Not?A_Brand";v="24"',
                'sec-ch-ua-mobile': '?0',
                'sec-ch-ua-platform': '"Windows"',
                'Sec-Fetch-Dest': 'document',
                'Sec-Fetch-Mode': 'navigate',
                'Sec-Fetch-Site': 'none',
            }
        )
        context.add_init_script("""
            Object.defineProperty(navigator, 'webdriver', { get: () => undefined });
            Object.defineProperty(navigator, 'plugins',   { get: () => [1,2,3,4,5] });
            Object.defineProperty(navigator, 'languages', { get: () => ['en-US','en'] });
            window.chrome = { runtime: {}, loadTimes: () => {}, csi: () => {}, app: {} };
        """)
        return browser, context

    # =========================================================================
    # TOOLTIP PARSING
    # =========================================================================

    def _parse_tooltip(self, text):
        """Parse tooltip text → (region, date_str, value) or None."""
        r = re.search(r'Port Region:\s*(East|West|Gulf)', text, re.I)
        d = re.search(r'Date:\s*(\d{1,2}/\d{1,2}/\d{4})', text)
        v = re.search(r'#\s*of\s*Vessels:\s*(\d+)', text)
        if r and d and v:
            return r.group(1).strip(), d.group(1).strip(), int(v.group(1))
        return None

    # =========================================================================
    # THREE-PASS PIXEL SCAN
    # =========================================================================

    def _pixel_scan(self, page, frame, box, x_start, x_end):
        """
        Highlight each region in turn and scan the chart pixel-by-pixel (right→left).

        For each x column, getImageData() identifies the vivid (high-saturation)
        pixel which is the highlighted line; the mouse moves exactly there and
        the tooltip is read. Per-region dedup prevents duplicate date entries.

        Returns: {date_str: {"East": val, "West": val, "Gulf": val}}
        """
        all_raw = []

        for region in ['East', 'West', 'Gulf']:
            logger.info(f"  Region pass: {region}")

            try:
                item = frame.locator('.tabLegendItem').filter(has_text=region).first
                item.hover(timeout=5000)
                page.wait_for_timeout(300)
                item.click(timeout=5000)
                page.wait_for_timeout(1500)
            except PWTimeout as e:
                logger.warning(f"  Could not select legend item '{region}': {e}")
                continue

            region_seen = set()
            hits = 0

            for x in range(x_end, x_start - 1, -1):
                pixel = frame.evaluate(_FIND_LINE_JS, x)
                if not pixel:
                    continue

                page.mouse.move(box['x'] + x, box['y'] + pixel['y'])
                page.wait_for_timeout(35)

                result = frame.evaluate(_POLL_JS)
                if result and result not in region_seen:
                    region_seen.add(result)
                    parsed = self._parse_tooltip(result)
                    if parsed:
                        reg, dt, val = parsed
                        all_raw.append(result)
                        hits += 1
                        logger.debug(f"    [{region}] x={x} {dt} {reg}={val}")

            logger.info(f"    {region}: {hits} tooltips captured")

        # Merge all three passes into {date: {region: value}}
        data = {}
        for text in all_raw:
            parsed = self._parse_tooltip(text)
            if parsed:
                reg, dt, val = parsed
                data.setdefault(dt, {})[reg] = val

        return data

    # =========================================================================
    # CSV OUTPUT (format expected by parser.parse_downloaded_csv)
    # =========================================================================

    def _save_csv(self, data, path):
        """Save scan results as UTF-16 tab-delimited file for the parser."""
        os.makedirs(os.path.dirname(path), exist_ok=True)
        with open(path, 'w', encoding='utf-16', newline='') as f:
            f.write("Scanned Data\r\nWeek\tTooltip\tIndicator\tValue\r\n")
            for ds in sorted(data.keys(), key=lambda x: datetime.strptime(x, "%m/%d/%Y")):
                for reg in ['East', 'West', 'Gulf']:
                    f.write(f"{ds}\t{ds}\t{reg}\t{data[ds].get(reg, '')}\r\n")

    # =========================================================================
    # PUBLIC API
    # =========================================================================

    def fetch_chart_data(self, last_date=None):
        """
        Load the BTS Tableau chart and extract vessel counts via pixel-scan.

        Args:
            last_date: datetime of the latest date already in master CSV.
                       None → full historical scan from x=CHART_X_START_FULL.
                       Provided → incremental scan from x=CHART_X_START_RECENT.

        Returns:
            str          — path to the saved CSV file
            "NO_NEW_DATA" — all captured dates are ≤ last_date
            None         — scrape failed
        """
        x_end   = config.CHART_X_END
        x_start = config.CHART_X_START_RECENT if last_date else config.CHART_X_START_FULL
        logger.info(
            f"fetch_chart_data: x={x_start}→{x_end} "
            f"({'incremental' if last_date else 'full history'})"
        )

        data = None

        with sync_playwright() as p:
            browser, context = self._make_browser(p)
            page = context.new_page()

            try:
                # ── Load page ─────────────────────────────────────────────
                logger.info(f"Navigating → {config.BASE_URL}")
                page.goto(config.BASE_URL, wait_until='domcontentloaded', timeout=60000)
                page.wait_for_timeout(6000)

                try:
                    page.click('a[href="#anchored-offshore"]', timeout=5000)
                    page.wait_for_timeout(3000)
                except PWTimeout:
                    page.evaluate("window.location.hash='anchored-offshore'")
                    page.wait_for_timeout(2000)

                # ── Find iframe ───────────────────────────────────────────
                logger.info("Searching for Tableau iframe ...")
                frame = None
                for _ in range(25):
                    for f in page.frames:
                        if config.TABLEAU_IFRAME_KEYWORD in f.url:
                            frame = f
                            logger.info(f"  Found: {f.url[:80]}")
                            break
                    if frame:
                        break
                    page.evaluate("window.scrollBy(0, 300)")
                    page.wait_for_timeout(800)

                if not frame:
                    logger.error("Tableau iframe not found")
                    return None

                page.locator(f'iframe[src*="{config.TABLEAU_IFRAME_KEYWORD}"]').first \
                    .scroll_into_view_if_needed()
                logger.info("Waiting 15 s for Tableau to render ...")
                page.wait_for_timeout(15000)

                # ── Verify frame loaded ───────────────────────────────────
                info = frame.evaluate("""() => ({
                    denied:   document.body.innerText.includes('Access Denied'),
                    canvases: document.querySelectorAll('canvas').length
                })""")
                if info.get('denied'):
                    logger.error("Access Denied inside Tableau iframe")
                    return None
                logger.info(f"  Frame OK — {info['canvases']} canvas(es)")

                # ── Locate canvas bounding box ────────────────────────────
                canvas_el, box = None, None
                for sel in ['.tab-tvView canvas', '.tabCanvas', 'canvas']:
                    for el in reversed(frame.locator(sel).all()):
                        b = el.bounding_box()
                        if b and b['width'] > 200 and b['height'] > 100:
                            canvas_el, box = el, b
                            break
                    if canvas_el:
                        break

                if not canvas_el:
                    logger.error("Chart canvas not found in Tableau frame")
                    return None

                logger.info(
                    f"Canvas: page_x={box['x']:.0f} page_y={box['y']:.0f} "
                    f"w={box['width']:.0f} h={box['height']:.0f}"
                )

                # ── Enable legend highlight mode ───────────────────────────
                logger.info("Enabling legend highlight mode ...")
                canvas_el.hover()
                page.wait_for_timeout(500)

                try:
                    frame.locator('.tabLegendPanel').first.hover(timeout=5000)
                    page.wait_for_timeout(400)
                except PWTimeout:
                    pass

                frame.evaluate("""() => {
                    var c = document.querySelector('.tabLegendTitleControls');
                    if (c) {
                        c.style.opacity      = '1';
                        c.style.pointerEvents= 'auto';
                        c.style.visibility   = 'visible';
                    }
                }""")
                page.wait_for_timeout(200)

                try:
                    btn = frame.locator('.tabLegendHighlighterButton').first
                    btn.hover(timeout=3000)
                    page.wait_for_timeout(200)
                    btn.click(timeout=3000)
                    page.wait_for_timeout(600)
                    logger.info(f"  Highlight btn: aria-pressed={btn.get_attribute('aria-pressed')}")
                except PWTimeout as e:
                    logger.warning(f"  Highlight button not clickable: {e}")

                # ── Three-pass pixel scan ─────────────────────────────────
                data = self._pixel_scan(page, frame, box, x_start, x_end)

            except Exception as e:
                logger.error(f"Scrape error: {e}", exc_info=True)
                return None
            finally:
                try:
                    context.close()
                    browser.close()
                except Exception:
                    pass

        if not data:
            logger.warning("No data captured from chart")
            return None

        # ── Incremental filter ────────────────────────────────────────────
        if last_date:
            new_data = {
                dt: vals for dt, vals in data.items()
                if datetime.strptime(dt, "%m/%d/%Y") > last_date
            }
            if not new_data:
                logger.info("All captured dates are already in master — no new data")
                return "NO_NEW_DATA"
            logger.info(f"Incremental: {len(new_data)} new date(s) beyond {last_date.date()}")
            data = new_data

        logger.info(f"Captured {len(data)} date(s) for downstream processing")

        path = os.path.join(config.DOWNLOADS_DIR, 'Scanned_Chart_Data.csv')
        self._save_csv(data, path)
        logger.info(f"Saved → {path}")
        return path
Now add the chart x-range constants and CONTINUE_ON_ERROR to config.py:

A better approach might be to match pixels against the expected color of each line rather than just picking the highest saturation.

The current system captures all tooltips regardless of region and merges them at the end, which means cross-region data gets added to the wrong pass—during the West pass, if an East tooltip appears at x=706, it fills East data correctly but leaves West data incomplete for that date.

The pixel scanner sometimes misidentifies which line is highlighted due to anti-aliasing or slight color value differences, causing it to pick up the East line even during West-highlighted mode. from datetime import datetime
prev = None
for w in weeks:
    y, wn = int(w.split('-')[0]), int(w.split('-')[1])
    if prev:
        py, pwn = int(prev.split('-')[0]), int(prev.split('-')[1])
        expected = (pwn % 52) + 1
        expected_y = py if pwn < 52 else py + 1
        if not (y == expected_y and wn == expected):
            print(f'  GAP after {prev}: next={w}')
    prev = w
print('Latest week:', weeks[-1])

Now I can clearly see the problem. The results: 28/41 fully complete — significantly worse than the best run we had (38/41).

Root cause analysis from the logs:

During the West pass, when the pixel scan finds the most-saturated pixel in a column, it sometimes lands on a different line than the highlighted one. Looking at the West pass log:

[West] x=706 y=390 rgb=(129,116,169) sat=31% → tooltip = 6/9/2026 East=2
[West] x=696 y=390 rgb=(129,117,170) sat=31% → tooltip = 5/12/2026 East=2
The RGB values match West's grey color during highlight mode, confirming these are the West line pixels. But Tableau's tooltip logic returns the nearest data point rather than the one directly at those coordinates — so even though I'm scanning the correct West line pixels, the tooltip that appears belongs to East instead.

At x=706, the East and West lines are vertically close together, and East's data point happens to be marginally closer to y=390 than West's, which is why the East tooltip fires. The real solution is to scan multiple y positions within each x column to find the correct tooltip that matches the current region I'm examining, rather than relying on a single y coordinate. : get the pixel with highest saturation first. If that doesn't yield the right tooltip, I'd try shifting the mouse position slightly up or down, or scanning a wider vertical range to find the target region.

I'm also considering a different approach: instead of prioritizing saturation, find the pixel whose color is closest to the known highlight color for each region—East's cyan, West's purple, Gulf's teal. The challenge is that West and Gulf have lower saturation values, making them harder to distinguish from the grayed-out lines.

Looking at the actual pixel data from the West pass, I notice something interesting: at x=706 and x=708, both pixels show the West line color, but x=706 triggers an East tooltip while x=708 correctly fires West. This suggests the East data point is positioned very close to the West line at x=706, so the tooltip system is picking up the nearer point.

The real issue is that tooltips fire based on which data point the chart considers closest in its internal coordinate system, not which colored line pixel we're hovering over. So even if we're visually on the West line, if East is slightly nearer, that's what appears. The solution would be to scan different y positions at each x column to find where the correct region's tooltip actually fires.

Modifying the approach... Writing the retry loop... Refining the search strategy by checking nearby y-coordinates to locate the correct region's tooltip when the initial pixel gives us data for a different region, then validating that we've found the right match before adding it to our collection. Refining the hunt logic to track captured (date, region) pairs and avoid redundant searches, then iterating through nearby y-coordinates to find the target region's tooltip at the same x position. I'll implement a y-sweep strategy: after finding the best pixel at a given x-coordinate, I'll move the mouse there and check what tooltip fires. If it's the wrong region, I'll scan vertically around that y-position in small increments until I find where the correct region's tooltip appears. This should resolve the hit-test contamination where East tooltips fire when targeting West data points. I'm realizing the issue might be that Tableau's tooltip proximity detection is based on the actual data point markers rather than the line pixels themselves. At x=706, the West line has a marker at y=390, but the East marker could be positioned closer to where we're hovering, causing the East tooltip to fire instead. I need to account for this marker-based proximity when searching for the correct hover position. This is how Tableau's tooltip detection works—it finds the nearest data point in a voronoi-based hit zone, regardless of which line you're hovering over. So the fix is to scan vertically around the pixel position until the correct tooltip appears. Since East and West have similar values, their y positions might be close, but scanning from y=380 to y=410 at x=706 should find a position where the West marker dominates the hit-test zone.

For efficiency, I'll scan ±30 pixels from the found y position in single-pixel steps—that's at most 60 attempts, which is manageable given the 20ms per step timing.

Implementing this... If we didn't find the right region at that position, I'm scanning vertically around the initial y coordinate to hunt for the correct one, testing offsets in both directions and checking each candidate against the target region before moving on. Refining the retry logic to check if we've already collected data for this date and region combination, so we only hunt for the tooltip if it's genuinely new information. Implementing the pixel scanning loop... Continuing the search logic...

I'm realizing there's a subtle issue with how captured_dates is scoped—it needs to be initialized once per region pass rather than per x-position iteration, otherwise I'll lose track of which dates have already been captured for each region. Let me trace through the logic to make sure the data structures are set up correctly. I'm realizing that captured_dates being reset per pass actually works correctly—when hunting in the West pass, it only checks whether West has already captured that date in the current pass, not whether East captured it earlier. And since all_raw accumulates across all passes, the data from finding West at a new y-coordinate gets added to the shared list.

The root cause is clear from the logs. The FIND_LINE_JS correctly identifies the West/Gulf line pixel, but Tableau's tooltip hit-detection fires for whichever data point marker is geometrically nearest — which at some x positions is a different region's point. At x=706 for 6/9/2026, the pixel IS the West line (rgb 129,116,169 sat=31%) but the East marker is slightly closer, so East tooltip fires.

The user wants to understand why 8/19, 9/16, and 2/17 miss East, and whether we can achieve 100% accuracy.

Let me analyze the logs more carefully. In the East pass, FIND_LINE_JS returned null for those x positions. This means at the x columns corresponding to 8/19, 9/16, and 2/17, no pixel with saturation > 0.15 was found.

But wait — in the West and Gulf passes, those dates ARE captured. So the East line IS visible on the chart at those x positions. The issue is that during the East highlight pass, the East line at those x positions has a saturation below 0.15 (our threshold).
I'm considering several reasons why the East line might have lower saturation at those specific x positions: anti-aliasing could be blending the line with the background, making it appear greyish; the thin 1-2px line might only occupy a single pixel at those spots which gets anti-aliased; perfectly horizontal sections of the line could render lighter; or the East values at those dates might align with chart grid lines, causing the grid color to dominate the pixel.

Looking at the test data more closely, I notice something revealing: at those three dates where East should appear, the East pass finds no saturated pixels, yet West and Gulf both register pixels with 27-32% saturation at those same x positions. This suggests the East line is either missing entirely or has saturation below the detection threshold at those columns, while West and Gulf lines are clearly present—which is odd since East should have much higher saturation (65-73%) when highlighted. OR the greyed West/Gulf lines at those x positions also don't have any pixels in the column at all—meaning the data points are positioned between pixel columns rather than directly on them. At those gaps between data points, the line interpolates but might not have a pixel that meets the saturation threshold exactly at that x coordinate. The East pass found 38 hits across x=580→740, but notably skipped 8/19/2025 entirely—its x range around 591-593 returned no pixels with sufficient saturation, even though the West pass detected a strong signal at x=593 y=385. This suggests during East highlight mode at x=593, the East line should be vivid (sat ~73%) while the West line gets grayed out (sat ~27-31%), yet FIND_LINE_JS is finding nothing there.

I'm checking the logic: the function filters for pixels where saturation exceeds 0.15 AND luminance stays below 230, then picks the highest saturation match. If the East line is present with sat=73%, it should definitely win that comparison—unless the East line's luminance is actually ≥230, which would disqualify it from the search entirely.

But the East color rgb(49,161,179) calculates to luma≈130, so that's not the issue. More likely, the East line at those specific x positions is either getting clipped by the boundary check (y < h-5) or is being obscured by the x-axis gridline which might have a brighter color overriding it.

Unless the chart is rendering differently during the East pass somehow.

The key insight is that tooltips fire based on proximity to data points, not just pixel color. So even if there's no colored pixel at a given x position, hovering there could still trigger a tooltip if it's close enough to a data point. The solution is to use Tableau's voronoi-based hover detection—when I can't find a line pixel at the exact x position, I can scan vertically at that x to trigger a tooltip for the nearest data point, since Tableau will fire tooltips based on proximity rather than requiring a direct hit on the line itself. The key question is whether the voronoi structure during the East highlight will actually capture 8/19/2025 East at the same coordinates where West was found, since the same spatial regions exist but with different region assignments based on what's highlighted. The highlighting only affects the visual display, not the underlying voronoi structure or tooltip behavior. So even when East is highlighted, hovering at (593, 385) would still show the nearest data point's tooltip—which could be West's 8/19 entry with value 3, the same result as the West pass. This means we'd capture a tooltip that's not in our East region set, but it wouldn't break the logic since we're just recording what appears.

Moving down to (593, 330) might reveal a different date entirely, like 8/26/2025 with East=12, which again wouldn't match our target. The real question is whether we can actually reach the East voronoi zone for 8/19/2025 at x=593—that depends on the vertical spacing between the East and West data points for that date, which varies based on their actual values and the chart's y-axis direction. the bottom of the chart where low values appear. I should implement a more thorough fallback by scanning the y-axis in smaller steps—maybe 30 pixels instead of 40—to catch these edge cases. That'd give me around 14 positions per column, which adds up to roughly 10 seconds per pass across all three attempts, still within acceptable limits.

I'll update both test_pixel_scan.py and scraper.py to add this fallback y-scan when a column returns no pixels. I also need to remove the input() call from the test file since it causes an EOFError in background execution—I'll replace it with a timeout instead.

Looking at the logs, the pattern is clear. For 8/19, 9/16, and 2/17 — FIND_LINE_JS returns null (no pixel found), not a wrong-region pixel. The East line at those x columns is anti-aliased/invisible at the pixel level. But Tableau's voronoi tooltip fires for the nearest data point regardless of pixel color — hovering blank space at those x positions would still trigger the East tooltip if we picked the right y.

The fix: when FIND_LINE_JS returns null, sweep y in coarse steps at that x and collect any new tooltips via Tableau's voronoi hit-detection. This is the "null column fallback."
